<Author>BrettNO
<Content>Extremely Pleased with The David - Great Owner and Staff My wife, 21-month old daughter and I stayed at The David in late November as we toured through Tuscany, Rome and Sorrento. The owner and staff were the friendliness and most helpful people that we have met in any hotel. They helped us plan all of our Florence and Tuscan ventures, and were always very friendly to us and our daughter (who loved to climb their stairs). They provided us with maps, advice, made car/wine tasting reservations for us and gave us guide books to borrow. The hotel is a very cozy place, parking is free, the happy hour is nice, and the breakfast was great. It is only a 10 minute walk to the center of Florence, so do not be deterred by the fact that it is not in the middle of town. If walking is not appealing, then you have a convenient bus stop directly outside the hotel. I would highly recommend this hotel to people looking for anything (romance, kid friendly, etc). Thank you to the owner and staff of The David!

<Author>MusicFoodTravel
<Content>A True Gem Generally I find the reviews on TripAdvisor over generous - a normal, solid hotel tends to be reviewed as the best, extraordinary and mixed up with our overall feelings of having had a good vacation, rather than something truly being an exceptional hotel. I myself am to blame for this as anyone and have generally avoided reviewing hotels now because of it.However, after just returning from a month in Italy, and staying at a number of places, both average and better, there was one hotel that really stood out, and merits the praise that it has been given.Hotel David is a very, very good hotel and worth your consideration when visiting Florence. It is not perfect, nor is it perfect for every type of traveler. If you want super luxury, Ritz Carlton accommodation, modernist, cutting edge architecture and electronic amenities, this is not your place. This is an affordable hotel costing less than 200 euro a night that has the right service to cost ratio.Instead, it is a very comfortable, carefully maintained villa near the Arno in a true neighborhood just outside of Florence's center, about a 20 minute walk away. The management clearly knows their clientele and has made some nice adjustments to meet their needs. It has larger, comfortable rooms with high ceilings, parquet floors, and characteristic 19th century styling and furnishing. (And you'll hear the upstairs guest footsteps if you're on a lower floor, but such is life with wood floors) The breakfast is quite good and very substantial, somewhat less typically Italian - it's more German in terms of selection and size. Fruit, cereals, yoghurt, fresh croissants and breads, meat, cheese, a savory tart, etc. in addition to both brewed coffee and espresso. There is a common room and patio, where each evening snacks and wine are offered in a comfortable setting.For a traveler like me, who tires of the tourist treadmill of cheap trinket shops, restaurants with lousy food, no locals and tourist menus in 5 languages, this hotel and its neighborhood is a welcome respite. It combines a homey (but not cheap and tired) ambience with nice touches of familiarity so foreigners feel welcome -- various foreign language newspapers, satellite TV with CNN and BBC, an excellent multilingual staff, free wireless network and free parking. There are a number of excellent restaurants in the surrounding neighborhoods, and the staff is quite helpful at pointing them out. They are true neighborhood gems, not touristy schlock. The staff is really outstanding. Multi-lingual, well trained, and truly helpful. They are ever ready w/ maps, suggestions, bus tickets, etc. So many thanks to the staff and management for a lovely, comfortable stay - this is a hotel worth keeping in mind by the independent traveler when in Florence.  
<Date>Nov 24, 2008

<Author>mwhitmoe
<Content>Wonderful Gem Across the Arno My new wife and I recently stayed there on our honeymoon. When we arrived at the hotel, we were greeted by Sabrina, who was charming, helpful and ebullient. There was a nightly complimentary happy hour which was already in progress (red and white wines , along with some fine finger foods).We were quite pleased with our room. It was extremely spacious, spotless, with some tasteful art. We were also thrilled to see that the hotel ha left us a bottle of wine to enjoy as a congratulations upon getting married. The complimentary wi-fi came in very handy for getting ideas about what to do in Florence. There was also a complimentary 10 minutes of phone use anywhere in the world per night using Skype. Originally we were scheduled to stay only two nights in Florence, but we loved the city and the hotel so much we stayed an extra two nights as well.The location of the hotel, while not ideal, is quite good overall. It is about a 20-25ish minute walk/stroll down the Arno river (a picturesque walk that I would recommend taking at least once when in Florence anyway) to get to Ponte Vecchio, the main pedestrian entryway to Florence. Alternatively, one can take a bus to Ponte Vecchio, for which the stop is just a block away from the hotel.My only bad experience was the final night. Our room was on the ground floor facing the main street near the hotel. At about 11:00ish, street cleaning began with a huge vehicle with flashing yellow lights that made a great deal of noise. For some reason it kept going up and down the street for almost FOUR hours. The curtains of our room were somewhat sheer, meaning that the flashing yellow lights could quite easily be seen reflecting off the walls and mirrors of our room. My wife was able to sleep through it all, but I was awake the entire time. Thicker curtains would be a nice upgrade.But that was the only issue I had while staying there. Sabrina and the entire staff is tremendously helpful (and all of them speak excellent English). Overall a wonderful stay. We will be back if/when we return to Florence!  
<Date>Nov 13, 2008

<Author>Curlicue
<Content>Great stay at the Hotel David I read many of the reviews on TripAdvisor before planning my trip to Tuscany and took a chance on the Hotel David. My boyfriend and I were not disappointed, it is a wonderful little hotel that is off the beaten path. The hotel itself is charming and has a comfortable sitting area on the ground floor where you can relax. As long as you don't mind walking a bit (15 Minutes) to get to the center of Florence where all the sites are, you won't mind staying here. The staff was extremely helpful (they recommended some good local restaurants near the hotel and the Palazzo Pitti and made reservations for us too). I noted that many people said their rooms were large - I will note that our room was quite small (Room 8 I believe), smaller than I would have hoped but it was not something to really complain about because it was immaculately clean and the bed was comfortable. The breakfast was quite good for one that is included. I think one of the biggest selling points of the Hotel David is that it is very quiet at night, you don't get any of the nighttime traffic noise that you would get at a hotel in the historic center and therefore are pretty much assured of a good night's sleep.

<Author>Bonhill08
<Content>Almost perfect The Hotel David is wonderful. The rooms are large, clean and very comfortable with a big and modern bathroom. The breakfast room is very nice and there is a lovely big sitting room on the ground floor with newspapers and magazines available for reading. The no charge use of a PC for internet access and the free onsite parking for our hire car were real bonuses but we were not able to take advantage of the free evening drinks that were offered - only because we were out at that time every day. Their other spectacular service was the provision of gluten-free breakfast items as a result of our advance enquiry - and not just ordinary gluten-free crispbread, but jam filled croissants as well as bread. And the standard breakfast was excellent. The staff were particularly helpful and gave a lot of good advice. The only downside is that the Hotel David is a 15 minute walk from the Ponte Vecchio so it is not easy to return to the hotel during the day, although having said that, it is almost on the river and public transport is very close, so it is not badly located.

<Author>LK59
<Content>Soooo Great! This was our best hotel in Italy. Great character and charm and the best people. I chose Hotel David thanks to great reviews here and I was not disappointed. Our triple room was spacious and clean, the hotel itself was beautifully kept - the owners just seem to care about the details. Happy Hour provided free wine and snacks and they even made a special dish when my daughter could not find something without cheese or milk in it (lactose intolerant). The only down side to staying here for a short stay is that it is a good walk from the center of Florence - but I loved being on the other side of the river. We had great weather, but a rainy or cold day would have made the extra walking a bummer. If I only had a night in Florence, I might opt for something in the heart of the city - just to keep it easy - otherwise, choose this hotel - you will not have any regrets.

<Author>First_timersPerth
<Content>Best hotel we stayed at in 5 weeks touring The best hotel we stayed at during our 5 week trip to Paris, Italy, London  Dubai. Our girls (6  11)and our friends also loved it. It felt like a home away from home. The reception staff freely offered info  advice (some other places we stayed was like pulling teeth to get info). The breakfast and happy hour staff were quietly efficient and provided homey and more than adequate food. They were constantly busy and met every demand for specially made coffees, hot chocolates - always with a smile and graciousness despite being under enormous pressure to keep the breakfast buffet topped up and tables cleared and re-set. Nobody could do enough for us - and all with a pleasant smile and can-do attitude (not with a forced smile and couldn't care less atiitude). The Happy Hours were excellent and gave us the opportunity to meet other travellers and share stories and tips. Our children met other children and happily 'explored' the hotel building and grounds and we knew they were safe (although the grounds really aren't that big).The breakfast room and lounge area were delightful (although breakfast could get a little crowded when groups wanted to dine at the same time). We felt safe in letting our children meet in the lounge area without us to chat, play chess and socialise. A digital photo frame is available to slip your camera card into so that you can see a slide show of your photos. Free internet was available and we were also allowed to make a free 10 minute call to anywhere in the world. Fortunately, nobody abused these services, so it's likely they will continue to be provided. However, must confess to over indulging at the Happy Hour as food, juice, wine  water were frequently replenished even when it was close to finishing time.Often no need for dinner afterwards! Our young daughter enjoyed it so much that by 5pm every day she made us rush back to the Hotel David so that we wouldn't miss the Happy Hour. Only drawback was that our room on the ground floor was noisy in the mornings as breakfast was being prepared and served.We could hear every footstep made by every person walking above us. However, if you are an early riser, this shouldn't be a problem. Our friends also had a shower curtain that needed to be held up by someone else while showering. However, they didn't consider it bad enough to complain as they enjoyed the Hotel David so much. Located on a very busy main road, but there is a car park and trees in front and shutters on all windows to buffer the noise. Note that this was not the swankiest or best furnished or most spacious hotel we stayed at, but it was the most comfortable, personable home away from home with little things that made us feel more than welcome. Definitely deserves it's current No. 2 ranking with Trip Advisor. If they provided a washing machine  dryer for guests to use it would be beyond perfect. We LOVE Hotel David.

<Content>If you had thought that Italian Hotel Staff Were Always Rude...... ..then the staff at the Hotel David in Florence will definitely change that impression....We stayed in the Hotel David for just one night, but it was definitely the nicest big city hotel we stayed at in all of Italy....The rooms were huge, even by North American standards, and very much gave the impression that you were staying in a traditional Tuscan villa (so long as you left the TV off)....Also, the staff were kind enough to allow us ot store our bags for 3 days while we Vespa-ed through Tuscany for no chanrge.....we had been afraid that we would have to store them at the train station, where we woudl undoubtably have been paying for the privelege of having rats gnaw on our belongings....Also, if they recommend going to a restaurant in the area, DO go to Trattoria da Beppino....The food is home-cooked, the proprieter is absoultely charming, and he gave us a bottle of Muscat with our dessert for free....If we do come back to Florence, and we will one day, we hope the Hotel David is still taking reservations!Laura

<Author>TripSavee
<Content>Great Small Hotel...away from the crowds !!! We just returned from a 4 night stay at the David; Mon. 10/6, then Thurs., Fri., Sat., 10/9-10/11.Our daughter, who is studying in Florence and staying with a host family in the Gravinana district of Florence, rode past this charming hotel on her way to/from school on the Piazza Savonarola.The location is central, but away from the crowds, which we accessed via a lovely drive on the Viale Michelangelo from the AutoEurope office downtown.I was coming down with a bug the first night and the wonderful young man at the desk gave me great advice on how to get to an eye clinic not far from the hotel. Our first room was on the main floor, (only one night), and we liked our second room much better, #20; ample, with plenty of storage, large bathroom and good shower, but also, great working air conditioning, as the weather was nice and warm during our stay in October.We were drawn to this hotel because of the TriAdvisor reviews, and also because we knew we would need parking, which the David not only offered, but made it extremely convenient to use; i.e., if you came in late and could not help but block another car, you simply left them your key and they would jockey the cars around. They closed their property gate at night, as the couple of eateries on the corner were popular for night life.The David is charming, safe, clean, ample, with a simple but satisfying breakfast, (we did not take advantage of the happy hour), and great staff, (I am sorry that I am unable to remember the names of the 2 lovely young ladies, two extremely helpful young men, and a delightful signora who let us in and out around midnight so we could drive our daughter to her homestay); they could not have been more accommodating. For my taste, I prefer to be outside of the tourist activity, yet close enough to walk or take public transportation to main attractions, and the David offered all that.I will not hesitate to refer the David to anyone traveling to Florence...thank you for a lovely stay !!!

<Content>Best italian hotel ever Simply one of the best hotel experiences we have had in over thirty years of travelling. Rooms large, clean, quiet with a helpful and pleasant staff. Comfortable lounge with plenty of reading materials and informative books. Free Internet access. Good breakfasts although the breakfast room can't seat all the guests if they turn up at once. <Author>srodrick1
<Content>Just Perfect! Stayed at the hotel David for 4 nights last week. The hotel is situated about 20 min walk to the Ponte Vecchio. If walking doesn't suit, there are 3 buses that stop outside the hotel. They offer a full continental breakfast, which is lovely and fresh espresso's or cappuccino's, which are to die for! Between 6.30pm and 8pm they offer a full range of nibbles ( bowls of pasta, bread and pate ), red/white wine and soft drinks. To be honest they call it nibbles but you could really have a two course dinner for free! This is to encourage guests to coverse with each other, and it really is delightful. We met some lovely people and had learnt some really interesting things! The room we had had a balcony looking over the garden, which I requested, and was very pleased. It is a bit noisy at night time, but that didn't bother us. We were that tired at night time from walking about all day, we could of slept through an earthquake! If this worries you, request a room at the back, but don't think they have balconies. The rooms and bathrooms are spotless and the shower is ferocious! Just what you need after a long day. The staff give a very personal service and even know what room number your in, so you don't have to keep asking when you get the key! Free internet access and 10 min calls worldwide a day. All in all this is a very special hotel. It is rated at a 3 star but to be honest is better thatn some 4 and 5 stars I have stayed in. Can't wait to go back. If your thinking about going to Florence, don't look anywhere else. Book hotel David NOW!

<Author>Amy920
<Content>A Wonderful Hotel! My daughter and I stayed at the Hotel David for seven nights earlier this month and couldn't have been happier. The location afforded us respite from the city center and every morning we explored areas of the Oltrarno on our walk across the river (about 15 minutes).The staff was, without exception, friendly and helpful. Our first night,feeling too tired to venture far for dinner, we were directed to a local restaurant/pizzeria (La Greppia), where we had a great meal (fantastic pizza). Gabriele, in particular, helped us with a number of issues. When we traveled to Lake Como in the middle of our stay, we simply left our large suitcases at the Hotel.The rooms are spacious, comfortable and clean. Breakfast is served in a light-filled and charming room, with a variety of both hot and cold dishes and many beverage choices. Cappuccinos are made to order. Free WiFi in the rooms was an unexpected bonus and there's an available computer in the lobby.I highly recommend the Hotel David to anyone looking for reasonably-priced and memorable accommodations in Florence.

<Author>tesoro08
<Content>Fantastic Hotel We had a wonderful stay at the Hotel David. The staff was extremely helpful and friendly. We were able to have them assist us with booking a reserved time at the Uffizi so that we did not have to wait in line for tickets. On our second day the staff helped us book a horseback riding excursion in the country. It was the best part of our stay in Florence! The website is listed below. www.horseridingintuscany.com. After riding, included in the price was a fantastic wine tasting a lunch at a local resteraunt in the castle. As for the room at Hotel David, it was extremely spacious and clean. The rooms really are sound proof as we were not able to hear the busy road outside our room. The water was warm in the shower and the complementary breakfast was lovely. The hotel is definitely off the beaten path but we prefer that, a 15 minute walk and you are in town. They have bus service outside not far from the hotel but we did not try that so I can't comment on how well it works. You must try the Fagioli resteraunt just in town, the staff will give you directions. It's amazing, home cooking by a family who has been in business since the 60's. We ate there twice! We would recommend this hotel to everyone. We had a great time and were extremely comfortable.

<Content>Loved the ambience We enjoyed 3 nights in this hotel. Our room was very roomy with charm - old character., the bed very comfortable , a safe is in the room, the daily cleaning was perfect. <Author>TJLandof10000lakes
<Content>Nice hotel with great service  Lots of good things to say about this place: free breakfast, free happy hour with hors dourves, free long distance calls using their Skype connection, free use of their internet-connected laptop, plus a very friendly and helpful staff ! The rate was very competitive. The room itself was large by European standards, very clean and had a comfortable bed. The room furnishings were quite ordinary. Noise from the street and/or rooms above could be heard (people walking on the wood floors, not voices)...not overly loud but enough that our sleep was just a bit disturbed. The location is a bit far from the heart of Florence (20 minute walk),  buses run frequently but with their schedule also take about 20 minutes. So, it's entirely 'doable' to stay here and enjoy Florence, but a place in the heart of the city would be more convenient. Overall, I would recommend this place as a clean, comfortable, affordable place to stay, with a very friendly and helpful staff !

<Author>Geordie_in_ABZ
<Content>Very Nice Little Hotel - Recommended We stayed in the Hotel David for 4 nights in August, having already had a few days in the Chianti area. The hotel is located on the edge of the city and what could be a nice walk into the centre of Florence can be a bit of a chore when it is 38C, as it was when we were there. However the hotel staff pointed us towards the bus stop just across the road where the small tourist buses run up to the Ponte Vecchio. They were also able to supply a map of the route and multi-trip tickets so no hassle with my non existent Italian.The David is a nice little hotel, the rooms are clean and the breakfast is very good. In the evening there are free snacks and wine in the garden, which is a nice touch and a chance to meet the other guests.However the best thing about the hotel is undoubtedly the staff. They are very helpful from the time you arrive to when you leave. The period when we were in Florence was the time when many of the restaurants close for the summer. However the staff not only suggested good places to go but also volunteered to phone and check that the restaurant was open and make a reservation. What is more when we returned they were keen to know if we enjoyed the meal etc.All in all I can thoroughly recommend it as a great place to have a relaxing stay in Florence.

<Author>DJSkippa
<Content>Lovely Hotel and staff, just more staff at breakfast please. Stayed here for 4 nights. Had a great welcome from a lovely girl as we walked in (sorry forgotten your name). Our room was big with two huge windows looking out of the front of this beautiful old building. Very helpful staff who supplied bus tickets and advice on where to eat. It is a bit of a walk into the city but walking in Florence is no effort. Regular bus drops you off outside hotel if you're tired. Only one criticism. There only appeared to be one member of staff on duty in the breakfast room. There are not enough tables for everyone and they are not cleared quickly so you have to wait whilst the one member of staff gets a free moment to do it. There could be a bit of a queue.This also meant that when the buffet was running low it was not replenished that often. I was unaware at first, but you could order an esspresso or cappucino from this one woman if you managed to catch her between jobs. We went to the cafe next door for a very nice and cheap coffee and danish on the last two days. My tip would be to eat and drink relatively near the hotel as the prices are nowhere near those in the city. Coffee in the City 拢5, outside hotel 拢0.90Having said that I would go back again.

<Content>Nothing but the best I don't know even where to begin. Before my arrival I worked with the hotel to book tickets to Uffizi and Academia and they responded promptly and graciously.. <Author>AlanWickersMoustache
<Content>Hidden treasure in Florence Staying at the Hotel David made our 6 day break in Florence every bit as memorable as visiting the Uffizi, the Duomo or Michaelangelo's David!! The hotel is an oasis of tranquility about 15 minutes walk alongside the Arno to Ponte Vecchio. High ceilings, marble floors, pleasant gardens all create the ambience of a Renaisance mansion. The staff were very pleasant and helpful - they will book train or bus tickets for you or recommend a local trattoria, which is popular with the local population and offers much better value than those in the heart of the city centre. Our two rooms were spacious with enormous beds, air conditioning, large bathroom with both bath  shower. The lounge is a great place to read the tourist guides, newspapers and magazines that they provide or even play chess!! WiFi is available throughout and you can use the hotel's PC in the lobby. They even give you one free ten minute phone call worldwide each day. The buffet breakkfast was everything you could want, fresh friut, cereals, fresh bread, boiled eggs etc.The hotel is not in the city centre, but if you can't manage the walk you can catch the bus ( D Service) outside the door to the Ponte Vecchio, which runs regularly till about 9.00pm. I would definitely stay here again.

<Content>A Great Choice We booked the Hotel David based on the terrific reviews on Trip Advisor and were thrilled with our choice. The hotel was just as we expected and the service was excellent. The staff is very helpful and friendly and made us feel right at home the moment we arrived.The breakfasts were varied and plentiful with delicious cappucinos made to order if desired. One night we did find it quite difficult trying to find a bus or even a taxi to take us back to the hotel later in the evening...I am not sure if the busses ran that late.All in all, a great time and we would definitely choose the Hotel David next time we visit Florence.

<Author>LeslieRMH
<Content>Great stay at Hotel David! We stayed at Hotel David for 3 nights in early July. We were extremely pleased with the hotel. The location was great: a bit off the beaten path, but within 15-20 minutes walking distance to Ponte Vecchio.The rooms were quite large and nicely appointed. Both of our rooms (a double for us, and a triple for our 3 kids) each had a balcony, with chairs, which we enjoyed. Breakfast was wonderful, and they were re-filling plates and pitchers even as breakfast was supposed to be closing. The evening 鈥渟nack鈥?was also a very nice touch, served in a lovely garden. We had a car, and it was wonderful to be able to park right at the hotel.The only issue we had was with the locks and keys. The doors can only be locked and unlocked from inside the rooms, with the key. Without thinking, we locked the door of our kids鈥?room and took the key with us. We did this in other hotels, which made it easy to wake them up in the morning, without banging on the door (they鈥檙e all heavy sleepers!). However, it turns out that they could not get out of their room! This could have been a serious safety issue. In fact, we locked our own room and, out of habit, removed the key from the lock. Had there been an emergency, we might not have been able to get out of our own room as well. The simple solution is awareness of the issue and to always keep the key in the lock. We mentioned this to the staff as we departed, and they were very receptive to the issue. I鈥檓 very surprised that we were the first to raise this issue.I would stay at Hotel David again without hesitation.

<Author>quin-i-bog
<Content>Top service at this small and friendly hotel! I stayed here with my husband and a friend last weekend. What a fantastic choice! Urged on by the Trip Advisor recommendations of good service we chose this hotel for our final weekend in Tuscany and it did not disappoint. From the second we pulled up in our hire car we were made to feel welcome and at home. The front of house staff are simply fantastic. They recommended great restaurants - and before we ventured out each day they checked our arrangements as there was a festival going on and not all activities and exhibitions were open as advertised. The staff phoned ahead, booked taxis, arranged tickets and did simply everything to make sure our days went exactly as planned. The hotel itself is in a cool, quiet part of Florence away from the hustle and bustle of the city centre which is a 15 / 20 minute stroll away along the banks of the Arno. If it's too hot to walk there are 2 bus stops just over the road and taxis arrive within minutes of being called. Our rooms were nice enough with window shutters and good air conditioning (essential!!) and all the amenities you'd expect in a 3/4 star hotel including king sized beds, mini bar and satellite TV. Breakfast is a cold buffet and the happy hour provides free wine / soft drinks and nibbles on the terrace between 6.30pm and 8pm. But it is the staff who make this hotel - I can't praise them enough - they were superb!

<Author>cgpit
<Content>Stolen Bag Just want to warn anyone staying at this hotel that we had a bag of ours stolen in the hotel lobby.When we arrived our room was not ready. The front desk clerk, a blond, told us that we could leave our bags in the lobby behind the couch and they would be ok. She told us if we wanted to go get something to eat and come back, our room would be ready.We were gone about 20 minutes and brought back our food to eat in the garden, right next to the lobby, where she suggested.We saw that she was starting to take our bags to the room so we got up to go in. When we got the to the room, my sister immediately noticed a blue bag, which had items she had purchased, as well as my niece's Louis Vuitton purse in it, was gone.We looked everywhere in the lobby. It was no where. There was a family checking out at the same time we came and we thought perhaps they took it by accident. The clerk said she would call the hotel they were going to in Rome and let us know if they had it. When we got back from dinner, she said they did not have it. We then spoke with the Hotel Manager, he basically blamed us. He told us we should have never left it in the lobby and then tried to say we left in the taxi. My sister, niece and nephew all saw the bag before we left for lunch. When we asked him about the hotel's insurance, he told us that since he was not 100% sure it was stolen, he could not file a claim. Again he tried to blame us for leaving it. When i told him that the front desk clerk is the one that told us to leave them, he then defended the hotel saying it was so safe he regularly leaves his wallet on the desk. When i confronted him about his contradicting himself by saying we shouldn't have left valuables, he turned red. He also said that the front door is always locked and someone is at the front desk at all times. This is absolutely not true. The front door was closed 1 time in the 4 days we were there and the front desk clerks regularly left the desk to either go outside or up to the eating area. He was completely unhelpful and made us feel responsible. We finally got fed up with his inaction and went to the local police station in Florence. The police officer who took the report immediately said that the hotel was violating basic rules by not having a baggage room to lock up bags. He also said the hotel should take responsibility for the stolen bag, as it was in their lobby and under their protection. He advised also to have their insurance handle it. I told him the Hotel Manager's response and he couldn't believe it. He told us to report this to the local Hotel Business Group that helps tourist who have experienced problems at hotels and pressures them to improve their standards. To make a long story short....DO NOT LEAVE YOUR ITEMS UNATTENDED NO MATTER WHAT THEY TELL YOU!!Unfortunately we had to learn the hard way at the cost of hundreds of dollars. The decent thing for the hotel to do was to reimburse us or atleast give us a night free. However, the only thing this Hotel Manager did was to blame us because they don't have basic security standards that any other reputable hotels have. The rooms themselves were nice but the breakfast was the worst we had in our 17 day stay in Italy. If you decide to stay here and your room in not ready, either wait with your bags in the lobby or take them with you!

<Author>thrall
<Content>Super staff! The best part of our stay at the Hotel David was the staff. They helped us find a lively trattoria for dinner. They tried so very hard to help me recover my cell phone. They host a convivial, generous wine and snack event in the evenings. They juggle multiple guests' needs in the small check-in area with aplomb.The second best part was the very fair price they charge for a room in Florence.Since one of our party has arthritis, the somewhat long walk (15-20 min., a bit over a mile) to the Ponte Vecchio made the location unsuitable for us. If you want to get away from the tourist maelstrom and the more unsavory parts of town, however, the location is great. It's almost on the river, has a small courtyard-garden, and has flower boxes in many of the windows.Our room was a bright shade of salmon, and the halls are adorned with small murals for trim, so the decor is cheerful. Our room was large enough, though not large, and the bathroom was clean, white tile with one of those tiny quarter-round showers that are ubiquitous in Italy. The room was quiet too.The common spaces are filled with comfy, overstuffed furniture and well-used by the guests. In general, the furnishings are older, some antique, some not. There is no glamour and no drama to this hotel, just homey charm.Breakfast was standard continental - coffee, juices, rolls, baked goods, ham, cheese, yoghurt. The lift is small and up a few steps, but serviceable.I would recommend this hotel.

<Content>Great Stay at the Hotel David! Our stay at the Hotel David was fantastic. The staff is extremely helpful, the most accommodating of any hotel on our trip in Italy. They were happy to make reservations, print train schedules, order a rental car, offer an itinerary for a day trip, and much more. <Author>Italotraveller
<Content>perfect stay in Florence Our family (2 adults, 2 children) stayed at the Hotel David for three nights. It was our first trip to Florence, and we couldn't have picked a better hotel. Our room was large for the four of us, impeccably clean, and the bathroom was a good size as well (especially the shower cabin). My kids liked all the hotel decorations, from the pictures to the wall stickers and the many books and magazines. The hotel staff has the friendliest and most helpful people I have encountered in a long time. They had good recommendations, they were energetic, and always willing to talk with a smile on their face. Happy hour was fun. My husband and I would enjoy a glass of wine, while our children played in the little garden outside.The location was excellent, right at the foot of Piazzale Michelangelo (best views over Florence). Every evening we would take a stroll up there. It takes 15 minutes to walk to the Ponte Vecchio, or if you are tired you could take the bus. Breakfast was good, the cappuchino was excellent. Hotel David is like a 4star hotel, and I wouldn't stay anywhere else in Florence.

<Author>luvtravel25
<Content>Unforgettable Hotel David is one of the six hotels we stayed at while in Italy. My husband agrees that this was the best of the six. The staff was warm and friendly- giving directions, making reservations and going above and beyond in every way. Sabrina was great! Florence was a very busy city and the hotel is walking distance to almost everything but away from the craziness. It was nice to be South of the Arno. Our room had tall ceilings, a great shower with hot water and good pressure and comfortable bed. Breakfast was good and presented nicely. I thought the coffee was nice and strong as well. Internet and happy hour make this hotel wonderful. We had quite the lively group one evening after happy hour and met some interesting people from all over the world. The hotel is on a busy street that leads up to Piazza Michaelangelo. You would never know it at night or sleeping in the next day as there was a button to push next to the window with an electric cork board that pulled down and closed out most sound and all light. I have nothing negative to say about this place. I hope their prices stay the same and that they continue the happy hour. As far as other advice I have to give- you HAVE to book a wine tour through Chianti and you HAVE to use Nathalie. She was so knowledgable and knew all the owners of the vineyards and castles and we got a behind-the-scenes tour almost everywhere we went. The owners chatted like old friends and handed the key over to her and we were free to explore the wine cellars of old castles and see where they make wine, balsamic and olive oil. She spoke English very well and had a great sense of humor. She picked us up from our hotel and drove us around for the day. She dropped us off in Greve to shop and took us to a family-owned place for lunch. Best day of the whole trip thanks to her (natintuscany@hotmail.com). I found her on tripadvisor. Restaurants- Gigi's was OK, Garden Room 15 euros for a drink!!!Ahhh!! That is a lot when the American dollar is performing so poorly. Il Latino had a neat atmosphere, but a long wait and the food was overrated. Our favorite was Osteria Antica Mescita San Niccolo. Walking distance from hotel and best cream of mushroom soup and a great beef and curry dish and good house wine. We loved the Boboli Gardens and wish we had spent more time there and would not have missed the view from the top of the Duomo. I know I got off subject here, but had to mention the few things that made our trip memorable. Overall, a wonderful 4 days and worth the exchange rate.

<Author>MrPH_8
<Content>P_H We visited Firenze in the beginning of April 2008. Because of a real chaos at Zurich airport we arrived to Hotel David at 1:00 in the night, 11 hours later than scheduled. The receptionist was very helpful and she even would have fixed us some coffee and something to eat in the middle of night, but we were very exhausted and only needed sleep. Our room was not very spacious but newly painted and the beds were comfort. There were no shelves in the bathroom, which was a real flaw. The towels were changed every day, which is not usual in every hotel. Also the room was cleaned daily. Sometimes we heard snoring from the neighbour room, but it did not disturb us.During our five nights staying the breakfast was much the same every morning. Just sufficient to start the day and keep the hungry away until the lunchtime. In some morning the waitress even asked if we liked to have cappuccino, which was not in the regular choice. A pleasant surprise was the wine and snacks service every evening. The reception staffs were very helpful and ready to give advises. They behaved very tactfully, never self-assertive, but always were willing to help whatever we asked. The hotel has own web pages www.davidhotel.com where you can choose one of 16 languages to check the availability and make the reservation. That is what I call a standard of service.The hotel locates in peaceful surroundings, not in the historical centre. Anyway, there are good bus connections if you don鈥檛 like to walk 15 鈥?30 minutes to reach the mainly tourist attractions.We enjoyed this decent hotel with obliging service, clean rooms and quiet nights to sleep. If we return Firenze some day, we surely check first the availability of Hotel David.

<Author>DrDave66
<Content>Excellent with Helpful and Friendly Staff My wife and I stayed in the Hotel David for three nights last week. The hotel is well situated about 20 minutes walk from the Ponte Veccio and is served by frequent buses to the centre of Florence (5 - 10 minute trip depending on time of day).The hotel is comfortable, clean and has lots of character and fantastic bathrooms. A buffet breakfast was included in our deal and had a variety of food to suit all tastes. There was also a happy hour in the evening (not sure if it is every evening, as we only availed of it once) with complimentary wine and snacks.The staff of the hotel were most accommodating and helpful. We arrived very late at night and were welcomed and checked in with the minimum of fuss. Staff at the reception desk helped us with transport timetables, directions and bus tickets, and arranged taxis when there was a short term bus strike. Highly recommended.

<Author>Magdelene
<Content>Great place to stay We stayed at the Hotel David after reading the reviews and I can say we were not disappointed. It is a lovely place to stay either for a weekend or longer. The rooms are lovely and of a reasonable size, we were on the front of the building and although a little noisy, because of the outside traffic, the double glazing kept most of the noise out. The lounge area was delightful, it was decorated and laid out as though it was a country house. The happy hour is free wine and nibblets which was fine if you wanted to meet the other hotel guests. Drinks can be ordered from the bar, albeit small, at a resonable price and later in the evening you pretty much have the lounge to yourself. The dining room, although small, was quaint and the breakfast was OK with plenty choice of continental food (No fry ups for the Brits but this is Italy so wasn't a problem for us). The staff were exceptional and, as commented in previous reviews, very helpful, a member of our party's luggage had been left behind in England (airport's fault, not hers) and the staff made many phone calls to assist her in locating the luggage once it had arrived in Italy. This hotel is truly a gem of a place and close to the centre. We tried the resturant, Gigi, round the corner as recommended by another trip advisor, but we found a better one (in our opinion) at the Ponte Vecchio bridge which served larger portions and tastier food. This was called Ristorante Alfredo sull'Arno, if anyone wants to try it out. Had absolutely nothing to complain about our trip and would recommend Florence and the beautiful Hotel David to anyone, we will most certainly stay there again the next time we visit Florence. An add on for the younger generation (as we were 45 to 57) this is not the place if you like an impersonal hotel or a hotel with some activity, however if you are into romance and are prepared to go out for a romantic meal then this is the place to be at a reasonable price.

<Author>Librarian757
<Content>A charming hotel My husband and I stayed here in December 2007 and loved it. It's a charming boutique hotel located south of the Arno River. <Author>Amit66
<Content>Loved Hotel David, will stay again We stayed for 2 nights at Hotel David this November when we were visting Florence. We were very satisfied with the hotel and specially the service at the front desk. They were helpful, courteous and spoke excellent English. The rooms and the bathroom were old but clean. Though the hotel is a bit far from the Ponte Vecchio, it is well connected by bus and you can buy bus tickets for the day right at the front desk. If you want to walk, its a 10 mins walk, not bad!! They also have reserved parking inside the hotel gates which we also found very convenient as we were driving through Tuscany. The hotel will also do all museum reservation if you request that when you reserve your rooms. They did our reservation for the Uffizzi and the Academia.

<Author>wittyone
<Content>Wonderful again !! My husband and I recently stayed at the Hotel David. This was our third stay in this lovely hotel. As always we were not disappointed. The quality of service was far above excellent as always. They have been doing some renovatiions, including some lovely improvements to the bathroom in our room. We were fortunate enough to stay in the same room as on our last visit. There is a lovely terrace for sitting in the mornings or evenings. Everything was spotlessly clean with wonderfully crisp and sweet smelling bedding. I always sleep well when I stay at Hotel David!! Breakfast again in the lovely breakfast room with Maria making wonderful capuccini has always been one of the highlight of our stays. There was a very good assortment of meats,cheeses,cereal,boiled eggs,rolls and delicious pastries along with the coffees and teas and juice. Maria herself is the gem of the breakfast room though !! The entire staff is always at hand to help us with all our travel needs. Bus schedules,train schedules,buying city bus tickets,restaurant recommendations and reservations,museum reservations--these are just a few of the services they provide with great detail and lovely smiles. The computer in the lobby is a lifesaver for many of us ! The early evening drinks and snacks in the parlour with a fire in the fireplace on cool evenings is another of the highlights of our stay at this hotel. We are always able to find other guests to talk to, to share ideas with and to learn from. This trip we even went to dinner with various people who were also staying there. One night we had a little party outside after dinner and they made cappucini and coffee for us. The hotel is not in the center of Florence but we always enjoy the walk along the Arno, or if not, it is simple to use a bus or taxi. There is a laundromat a few blocks away that we always make use of. There is a little grocery/meat market next to the laundromat where we always purchase our cheese and wine to bring home. Our favorite trattoria, Trattoria GiGi's, is located across the street from the grocery store. There are at least three or four other places to eat in this area and all are very good.The owner, Gabriele Cecioni makes certain that the hotel and the hotel staff meets and exceeds very high standards. He is a wonderful man and it is always a delight to find the time to chat with him. His wife is also quite lovely and charming. And I can't forget to add that their son Marcco (one year old) is simply adorable !We have become accustomed to measuring the comfortability and quality of service at other hotels by the standard that we have known at Hotel David. Not many even come close. We will never stay anywhere else in Florence as long as the Hotel David has a room for us.Thank you to Signore Cecioni,Michele,Sabrina, Serena, Maria and to all the others at the hotel. Thank you for making Florence like a second home for us. Thank you for caring about your customers. You are all always in our hearts.

<Author>leighlee0829
<Content>I'll stay here again I'd give everything about this hotel high marks. It's location is perfect -- it's far enough outside of the bustling tourist center to feel like a refuge, but within easy walking distance of the Duomo, Uffizi, and other major sights. The hotel is also a short walk from Piazza Michaelangelo, which provides some pretty spectacular vistas of Florence. Our room was comfortable, quiet, and nicely appointed, and I loved the deep bathtub (perfect for a long soak after walking around all day -- although you should note that not all rooms have bathtubs. We just got lucky). In the morning, there's a huge spread for breakfast (included with your room cost) with cakes, pastries, coffee, juices, cereal, fruit, meats, and cheese. Staff will even make you a cappuccino if you ask. In the evening, there's a lovely set-up with free wine and snacks in the common room. Other nice touches: free wifi in all of the rooms; courtesy umbrellas by the door that you can borrow if the weather turns; a cozy common room with a fireplace; lots of periodicals and novels lying around for you to read (quite a few in English -- and good stuff. I saw both National Geographic and a Jose Sarramago novel); and a little bar off to the side where you can get a glass of wine or cappuccino for one euro any time of the day. The staff was also friendly and helpful -- they'll make your reservations for the Uffizi and Academie (to see David) upon your request, and on our last day, allowed us to leave the car in the parking lot after we checked out so we could see a few more sights without having to deal with the hassle of moving the car (and the risk of parking it in a public place w/ our luggage inside). A spotless, comfortable room and top-notch service -- I'd definitely stay here again.  
<Date>Nov 25, 2007

<Author>SanKookai
<Content>Excellent hotel We have just come back from our holidays in Italy. We stayed at Hotel David for 5 nights before moving on to Venice. This was the best hotel of the two. I picked Hotel David after reading reviews on this website and I was not disappointed. We had room 18 on the second floor. Our window opened to the back of the hotel and was very quiet. The hotel is situated near a very busy roundabout so it might not be so quiet in every room. Our room was very big and extremely clean. I cannot stress enough how helpful the staff was. We had a bit of a problem with our flight and arrived at midnight instead of 17:30. There was someone to great us and give us all what we needed for our first night as of course our luggage never turned up. They offered to help us to phone the airport and deal with our lost luggage but it arrived the following day.They provided us with a plug adaptor and a map of Florence with lots of info regarding where to take various buses to visit the sites. They also gave us excellent advise for restaurants. They always took time to answer our questions and have a little chat.We enjoyed walking around this part of the town as it felt more the real Italy. There are lots of small shops nearby and not that many tourists around.It takes about 15-20 minutes to walk from the hotel to the Ponte Vecchio. I would suggest not to walk along the river (maybe the first time as you can see the bridge and other sites from there) but there is quite a lot of traffic on that road. Just a street away, you can enjoy much more quieter streets with again lots of small shops that gives a good insight of people's way of life. Those streets also take you by very old houses and palaces that you would not see otherwise.Finally guests can use the Internet free of charge every evening from 19:30 to 22:30. This was a great way to check our emails and let people home know about what we were up to.On the whole, our stay at Hotel David was brilliant and we would go back there with no hesitation.

<Author>EnglandExpects
<Content>Charming hotel with charming staff Well, what can I add to all the great reviews of this hotel? It really is charming and the staff are a delight making the stay even more enjoyable.The hotel is beautifuly furnished with laminated floors and half-marbled walls and staircase. The upper walls are white-washed and charmingly decorated with all sorts of painted animals and insects adding a touch of humour. A buffet breakfast sets you up for the day and there is a happy hour laid on by the hotel from 7-8pm with free wine and nibbles. No restaurant, but you don't soak up the cuisine and ambience of a city you visit by dining in the hotel anyway.The hotel is located on the Piazza Ferrucci which is on the south bank of the Arno, east of Ponte Vecchio. I recommend 3 ways of getting there until you get your bearings: by taxi; by bus D that goes back and forth between the train station and Piazza Ferrucci or simply by walking east along the south bank of the Arno until you reach Piazza Ferrucci. Don't do what I did on arrival which was to get to the start of the Via Michelangelo at Piazza Michelangelo and then find the hotel is right at the other end of that road!Florence is beautiful, especially if you're a fan of Renaissance art like me. It's like walking back into the 16th century with all the medieval streets and that's particularly reflected in the hotch-potch condition of a lot of the architecture, such as the Ponte Vecchio which appears in so many photographs but is really a bit of a muddled, propped up shambles. All adds to the charm though. Enjoy!

<Author>ManjuCake
<Content>Charming Oasis in Bustling Florence We spent three nights at this cute, charming hotel located on a gated property. Everything about the hotel was excellent. We were given a good-sized room with a wonderful terrace. Though our room faced a very busy thoroughfare, the windows and shades (which are drawn electronically) insulated us from any street noise. We slept very comfortably. The air conditioning was excellent. The bathroom, very smartly decorated and immacuate, was a bit on the small side as it had limited places to put things. No big deal though. The shower was really excellent. Lots of constant hot water, good pressure from the shower head.The front desk service was truly extraordinary. Everyone was extremely friendly and exceedingly helpful. They made excellent restaurant recommendations near the hotel as well as in the downtown area. If you don't enjoy walking, but want to be near the Duomo, it is a bit of a hike from the hotel (maybe 40 minutes). This could be a problem if you want to go back and forth from the hotel. It's not that far to the Ponto Vecchio (about 20 minutes each way), but after a long day of walking, going back to the Duomo area for dinner can be daunting. A cab ride from Hotel David on a busy Saturday/Sunday night can be 18+ euros one way. Fortunately there are a lot of good neighborhood restaurants that the hotel can recommend, many of which are located just down the street from the hotel or about a 5-7 block walk outside the old city walls. You can also take the city buses to and from the Duomo. Hotel gave instructions on how to do this.Overall, Hotel David is an excellent value. I highly recommend it and would most definitely stay there again.

<Content>Absolutely loved the Hotel David My husband and I stayed at the Hotel David in Florence (13 August to 16 August) during our 18 day trip to Italy. The Hotel David lived up to all of the accolades I had read on TripAdvisor. The hotel is located on the far side of the River Arno, a quick ten minute bus ride to downtown Florence. Bus stops are conveniently located just outside the hotel鈥檚 door and stop there every ten to 15 minutes. (The hotel even sells bus passes鈥攕o convenient). We stayed in a large room with comfortable bathroom, where we enjoyed peace and quiet each evening. (No trouble getting to sleep there!). I should point out that a remote control allows you to regulate the air conditioning, so do be on the look-out for that item. It certainly comes in handy in August! We enjoyed our breakfast there 鈥?a traditional fare of breads, coffee, fruit, and cold cuts. And, their afternoon happy hour (5:00 p.m. to 7:00 p.m.) was delightful. We enjoyed relaxing with a glass of wine on their outdoor patio with other guests. Don鈥檛 miss a late afternoon stroll from the hotel to the top of Piazza Michelangelo to watch the sunset over Florence. You鈥檙e in for a real treat if you stay to see the sunset 鈥?something not to be missed. It鈥檚 only a ten minute walk (uphill) from the Hotel David. I would be remiss if I didn鈥檛 mention how helpful the staff at Hotel David was. Via email, they set up our reservations for us to see The David and go to the Uffize. (Be sure to make reservations 鈥?the lines are very long without them). The staff always asked where we were going each morning and provided us maps to guide us. It鈥檚 hard to describe how helpful they were in guiding us around their lovely city. Frankly, they really made you feel at home鈥攚hich was a most welcome feeling. Hotel David provides its guests free Internet access on a lobby computer. If you have a laptop with you, you can also access their wireless Internet network, using a password that the staff will provide you. By using our Touring Club Italiano Card [--], we received a 15% discount on our standard room rate (E99, bringing it to about E85 a night). If our travels take us back to Florence, we will happily stay at Hotel David.

<Author>MD_scubanut
<Content>A low cost gem! My wife and I stayed for three days during our honeymoon and the Hotel David was a great find. The location of the hotel is excellent and within walking distance of all the downtown Florence tourist sites including the Ponte Vecchio, the Duomo, the Uffizi, and the Accademia Gallery. I would advise having a pair of comfortable walking shoes if you plan to travel on foot, but it will help to burn off all the great Italian food! The Hotel David is very clean and the staff are quite helpful if you need some assitance in locating anything around the city. We were very happy with the large room and tiled shower that was big enough to accommodate a 'full sized' person. The room was air conditioned, which was a blessing during the warm weather in July. We initially requested the room with a balcony above the garden, but we found that the noise level was a bit high from the traffic outside (and the room smelled of cigarette smoke), so the staff relocated us to a very nice room on the interior of the hotel (no view, but nice and quiet). We especially liked the free happy hour that the hotel would put on every evening. Free red and white wine and light snacks were offered. We met some really nice folks from Ireland, Australia, and California during our stay as we all sipped wine in the garden. This was a nice added touch that allowed us to get to know the other guests at the hotel and learn about where they came from. The hotel also has a single Internet point that guests can use for no extra charge. Wireless internet is available if you need Internet access in your room. The complimentary breakfast in the morning is good for the price of the room. We had better breakfasts at other hotels, but we also paid significantly more for a nighly stay.We would definitely stay at the Hotel David again if we are lucky enough to visit Florence, which is a beautiful city that should not be missed. The Hotel David is economical, convenient, and clean. You won't be disappointed.

<Author>devildog820
<Content>Very Nice Hotel With a Great Staff My wife and I stayed at the Hotel David and we absolutely loved it. It is located across the river from the old city (10-15 minute walk from the Ponte Vecchio or 3 minutes by bus). The room we stayed in was very large, especially by European standards.The hotel and room was very clean. The air conditioner worked very well and we were never uncomfortable. The breakfast was awesome; the staff will make cappuccini for you and the food was very good.The staff at the hotel were outstanding. Everyone from the property manager to the night clerk (whose name I can't remember) were very helpful. We must have had the girl working the night desk help us ten times over our stay and she was very polite and helpful.The hotel is on a really neat property. They had free parking (which we didn't use) and a cool garden where they did a happy hour every day. The happy hour included red and white wine as well as little pizza bites and cocktail mixes. It was fun to come back after a day of walking everywhere and have some wine and snacks before heading out to dinner.I would highly recommend this hotel to anyone staying in Florence.

<Author>seadawg
<Content>Hotel David Lovely Place to Stay Hotel David was lovely in every way. None of the other places we stayed in Italy on a month-long visit came even close to the comfort, cleanliness and thoughtful care that goes into this hotel by the owners and staff. The lovely air-conditioned rooms, nicely furnished and gorgeous sheets, comfortable beds, spotless bathrooms and amazing breakfasts, made our trip to Florence special. Their website doesn't really show the nice open shared areas and verandah that make the hotel a stand-out. The midday snacks and drinks were a nice touch and we appreciated the computer station. The owners and front desk personnel were amazing. Answering all our questions and helping us with ideas for dinner, etc. I just wish we were in Florence longer! The hotel is a little out of the main area, so it is very quiet, walking is no problem, but if you can't take long walks, the bus service is good. We did take a cab one night when we were out late and exhausted. But if you have a car, parking is free at the hotel.

<Author>Christine47
<Content>Excellent Choice Like all the other reviews, we found the Hotel David to be excellent. The Hotel is a 20 minute walk, along the river, from the Centre but we found this to be no problem. If you don't fancy the walk, several different buses can be caught from almost directly outside the Hotel. On arrival, we were greeted warmly, with our cases being carried into reception. Our bedroom was spacious, quiet, spotlessly clean and very comfortable. The Hotel offers complimentary drinks and nibbles in the early evening which was the perfect way to start our nights out, before wandering to the Centre to enjoy the wide choice of restaurants and bars available. We particularly liked the excellent-value little Trattoria Cibreo on 122r Via de Macci. Very enjoyable with a most helpful waiter, willing to translate the menu into English. There are a couple of restaurants local to the Hotel but its well worth going to the Centre in the evening, as the choice is much better. Also nice to see the Duomo and the other amazing landmarks after dark, and without the day-trippers. As two women travelling alone, we felt quite safe walking around the city at night. Common sense with carrying bags etc., must prevail at all times. For a local drink, we would also recommend bir Bacco on Lungarno Ferrucci, just around the corner from the Hotel David. Very pleasant atmosphere with charming bar Staff. Good experience.Anyone looking for accommodation in Florence, with beautiful surroundings, very caring, friendly Staff, good choice of breakfast and every whim catered for, could do no better than the Hotel David.

<Author>cab33141
<Content>A Great Suburban Hotel in Florence We just finished a 15-day tour of Italy, including a 4-day visit to Florence. The Hotel David was our home in Florence, and we were very happy with the hotel and the service they provided us. This hotel has a suburban, out-of-the-city look and feel to it-which I think is one of its assets. It's about two miles from the Ponte Vecchio, the Uffizi Palace, and the other cultural focuses of Florence, and is in the quieter and much newer western suburbs of the city. There's a delightful garden that surrounds the hotel which quiets and softens the place, and the ambience is small, rural, country inn. While there is some three-lane traffic about 100 yards away, the general mood is restful and quiet. We used the D-bus-a local people hauler with a stop just outside the hotel- to commute back and forth to the Ponte Vecchio bridge, and this made access to downtown easy and quick. Accomodations were bright, clean, quiet, and comfortable. The front-desk staff, and the dining room staff were all very helpful, friendly, and full of great tips on the local sites and entertainment. I feel they all went out of their way to make us feel comfortable and welcome. The breakfast provided daily was very nicely presented, tasty, abundant, and filling. We definitely reccommend this hotel! We found it a welcome respite from the crush of tourists and crowds, and a great place to get some rest after a hard day of touring the city.

<Author>hawkeyes
<Content>Deserves Its Ranking This is a great little hotel. The service was superb, our room clean, suitably large, comfortable and quiet, overlooking the back yards of adjoining homes. Breakfast was pretty standard for Italian hotels, served by friendly staff who made Lattes on request! The hotel is not downtown but is a twenty minute walk from the city core. You can get a bus right outside the door that will take you to the Ponte Vecchio. From there it is a short walk to the main atractions. The hotel booked our reservations at the Uffiziz and the Academia. Reservations ar an absolute must if you do not want to stand in a line for hours. There is an Internet site. The hotel has a happy hour where you can meet some of the other guests in the salon. Very nice. The hotel is moderately priced and really deserves it high Trip Advisor rating.

<Author>TerpTraveler55
<Content>A pleasant surprise! My family and I (wife, 17 year old son and 70+ year old in-laws) spent 2 nights at the Hotel David last week. During our Italian vacation, we stayed in Milan, Rome, Florence and Venice and we found the Hotel David to be the best hotel of the bunch!The hotel is on the southern side of the Arno River, so you are a little away from the heart of Florence, but it was very easy to get around as a taxi stand was just outside the hotel. The hotel sits on charming lot with a small, shaded garden terrace just outside the main floor. There is another elevated terrace on the back side which is much sunnier. The lobby area opens up to a very comfortable living area with books, magazines, newspapers and a chess board. The entire hotel is decorated beautifully and its overall charm makes you feel very comfortable.The rooms were spacious and very clean. The bathroom was surprising large with a nice high-powered shower. The beds were comfortable and the linens were clean and soft.For the price, this was an absolute gem. But the best part of the stay was the very friendly and helpful staff. Every member of the Hotel David staff was extremely welcoming. They made us feel right at home and even went out of their way to ensure our room was fine -- they allowed us to look at a couple of room choices before we settled in.If you want a small, charming, clean, quiet and comfortable stay in Florence -- choose this hotel. Once you arrive, the staff will make sure you made the right choice!

The room was clean. This hotel is also not that far from themain part of town, of course if you don't like to walk to much, it may be for those. We walked around town a lot and walking from the center of town to the hotel was not bad at all- it was beautiful walking around Florence. We love this hotel that whenever we go back to Florence (which I am sure it will happen again), we will definitely consider staying here. We love the wine  snacks in the afternoon that the hotel provides for the guest. It was a delight.

<Author>Hollander
<Content>A quiet and clean resort in a bustling town My wife and I just returned from a two day stay at the Hotel David in Florence. We had booked the room through their by the way excellent website that surprisingly enough was also available in almost flawless Dutch.Anyway, the hotel is located near the 'old centre', close to Piazza Michelangelo, basically 50 meters south from the river Arno.The plusses:Friendly and helpful staffFree WiFi internetCleanAtmosperic vintage decoration, homely feel and well maintained roomsFree parkingPretty easy to reach by carPublic transport to the centre very nearbyA good shower (pretty unique is our experience)There is a bar and Rosticceria just around the corner for people who want a quick bite or eat inside the roomPretty good breakfastGoing by foot to the centre will take you about 30 minsThe minusses:In that area itself is not much going on, it is not the heart of the centre of Florence. Some people might be turned of by this.Though parking is free, space is very limited and you will have to turn in your car keys when not needed, so the hotel staff can 'valet service' cars that block other parked cars.In short, unless you really want to stay in the heart of Florence, this hotel is an absolute gem and we can highly recommend it.

<Author>caroyak
<Content>Wonderful  We just returned from a 2 1/2 week trip to Italy, 2 nights of which we spent at Hotel David in Florence. We LOVED it! While the hotel is not directly located in the heart of the city, it's extremely close and easy to reach, both when arriving to the city (via car) and traveling to the historical district. It's a very short block from the Arno and on several public bus lines, so it's very very easy to get anywhere you'd like to go. If you're a walker, you can reach Ponte Vecchio in about 15 minutes, strolling along the river on a lovely paved path.The hotel staff could not have been more welcoming. The staff was very friendly and extremely helpful from our arrival until departure. On arrival, we were given a 1 page map of the city with all major attractions clearly marked (and a huge star marking the hotel location). Reception then drew out the route of 2 bus lines (marking the stops) that they recommended to easily reach all major sites (Duomo, Uffizi, etc).Our room was very large (particularly by European standards, but pretty large by American standards as well IMO) and spotlessly clean. The room decor was tasteful and simple - antique wood desk, huge wall armoire/closet, TV (CNN/BBC were only English speaking channels we noticed), mini fridge/bar, huge windows overlooking a courtyard (no view obviously but nicely private), and huge marble bathroom with everything you would need.Free parking was also available - inside the hotel gate - very nice bonus since it can be very expensive  difficult to find.Breakfast in the morning was delicious - typically some pastries (croissants, etc), rolls, cereal, fruit, coffee, tea, juice, yogurt.There is a lift, but it's teeny tiny  kinda shakey. We're skinny  we barely wedged ourselved  2 bags in there for the ride up!Overall, it was our favorite hotel in Italy! The staff were very kind, everything was kept very clean, the decor was cute and the location was perfect.They claim to be a 3 star hotel, but i think it's more like a low 4 star.Don't hesitate to stay here :)A++++

<Author>TransylvanianGrl
<Content>What a wonderful place! Last year I stayed with my parents at Hotel David and we couldn't have been happier with the accommodation. I wrote a review right after our trip, but it never showed up on TA. I hope this one will! Lovely, friendly people at the reception desk (always ready to answer questions), fabulous breakfast (which set us up for walking for several hours), great cappuccinos made to order for breakfast. The room was spacious, with three beds (two of them very comfortable, one a bit too soft), good AC (it was wonderful to return to a cool room as we were in Florence during a heat wave). Large bathroom and good, absorbent towels. We liked having the mini-fridge in the room and the safe. Some people seem to think that it is far away from the center of Florence, but we actually enjoyed the 15 minute walk in the morning and then back in the evening. We took different routes--the best was the return with a detour by Vivoli. Yum!We will definitely be back! It is my favorite hotel in Italy and I have tried quite a lot of them in the same quality/price range.

<Author>DaveFromKC
<Content>Overall, An Excelent Choice The Hotel David was the best hotel we stayed at during a two week trip. The room was quite large with a balcony. Breakfast consisted of sweet croissants (cornettos), fresh baked rolls, deli-ham, cheese, yogurt, cereal, fresh fruit, orange juice and coffee. Evening snacks were pizza slices, olives, peanuts white or red wine or orange juice. Everything at the hotel was just like all the other reviewers stated. I did well by reserving through the hotel's web site. I got a cheaper rate and I got a package which included a wonderful tratoria lunch near Ponte Vechia. Lunch was two plates (Plate one was a choice of five pastas, plate two was a meat and vegetable dish). Dessert, wine and bread included. I even got 5% off my hotel rate just because my name was David.If you arrive by train at SMN station it can be a little tricky getting the bus to the hotel. First, buy a few bus tickets at the bus office just outside the station. It is cheaper than buying on the bus and saves alot of hassle. Disregard the sign for bus #23 by the bus office since it is going the wrong direction. Instead, walk past the taxis in front of the station and cross the street to a major bus stop. Wait for bus 23 or 23A. it should come by in ten minutes or less. Once on the bus stamp your ticket. The bus will first swing by the Duomo before crossing a bridge over the river. Once you cross the bridge, it should be the third stop (I think). Look for Orsini on the bus stop sign. The hotel is right around the corner from the cafe. If you need a few items from a grocery store it is a ten minute walk across the bridge in front of the Hotel David to COOP supermarket. Ask at the front desk for a map and directions.  Florence is truly a very beautiful city. Just allow at least three full days just to hit the main sights. One thing to be forwarned about are the professional beggers. They seem to be all over the touristy areas. I got a kick out of one older lady whose territory is the Ponte Vechia. Every time I walked over the bridge there she was walking around saying grazzi in a raspy voice. You can't miss her.All in all, the Hotel David is an excelent choice!

<Author>Otis_Clarence
<Content>Another Recommendation for the David!! We chose the Hotel David for our stay in Florence due to the wonderful reviews on TripAdvisor and were certainly not disappointed. In fact, it was one of our favourite hotels throughout our travels. We enjoyed the peace and quiet of the residential area in which the hotel is to be found and the short walk along the river to and from the centre of the city. There is a bus stop across the road from the David which goes directly to the train station, which we found very convenient. Our room was large, impeccably clean, tastefully furnished and had French doors that opened onto a small balcony. The staff were always friendly and helpful, more than happy to accommodate any question or request. We were recommended the nearby GiGi Trattoria and we had a wonderful meal. We can also highly recommend the Rosticceria around the corner- perfect for a picnic lunch! The staff of the David organised advance tickets to the Accademia museum which saved us a lot of time waiting in line. The breakfast selection was extensive, delicious and served with a smile- a great start to the day!We will definitely return to the David on our next holiday and would recommend it to anyone looking for a charming and serene haven in Florence.

<Author>Deb_and_family
<Content>3 star hotel with 5 star value! The Hotel David in Florence is so wonderful, I could easily run out of adjectives to describe it. Located on the opposite side of the Arno River, it's blessedly devoid of tourist mobs (and noise!), but still within walking distance of all the major sights - plus a few you might overlook, staying in the more centralized areas.My husband, daughter and I recently enjoyed a 5 night stay, and here's what we experienced for around 95 euro a night: a beautiful, *huge* room with a king-sized bed for hubby and I, and a lovely sleigh bed for my daughter; ensuite bathroom with heated towel racks, a bathtub and shower, and complimentary hair dryer; double French doors leading to a small balcony overlooking a lovely outdoor sitting area; in room TV, phone, mini-bar/fridge and safe; free WiFi in our room (and complimentary Internet connectivity at the workstation in the lobby); a spacious lounge area downstairs filled with travel books and plenty of brochures on sights and activities in and around Florence; nightly happy hour with complimentary wine/beverages and snacks; a gorgeous breakfast room with a yummy selection of food and beverages to start your day off right; an in-house bar with a really good wine selection, and close proximity to great restaurants, shops, food markets, a Bancomat, tabacchi, bus lines,and taxis.The very best thing about the Hotel David, though, was the outstanding staff. Every single person, from the front desk people, to the young lady who prepares breakfast, to the maids, are overwhelmingly friendly, cheerful, helpful, and go way beyond the call of duty to make your stay in Florence as pleasurable as possible. I'm sorry I wasn't aware of this hotel last year when I visited Italy - but now that I am, I wouldn't dream of staying anywhere else. Grazie mille, Hotel David!

<Author>tennsurfr
<Content>Lovely hotel, great $$ bargin, but not clcose to attaractions We picked this hotel strictly on recommendations found on Trip Advisor.The good things are all here - friendly owners, nice people, about 90% English speaking, decent breakfast (just OK, really), and what all the other reviews say. However, after a long day of trekking, the hotel is not conveniently located. That's probably why the rates are so attractive. It cost us avg. 8 Euros each way to the center of town. The buses are crowded and not punctual.So, in your minds, add another 16 Euros at least to the daqily cost of staying at the David. Don't get us wrong...Uffizi and Accadamie are unbelievable. Ponte Vecchio is bustling with the peddling of higher end jewelry. The Arno river is dirty looking and not very scenic at all. To us, this is not the mecca others describe.This was my 6th trip to Italy over 25 years. I find it a constant grind, tiring and not always rewarding. I doubt we'll be back again.Actually, we found the people much nicer (surprise, surprise) and the food much better in France.

<Content>Wonderful Small Hotel We stayed at this charming hotel for 7 days and were totally happy with our choice. We had a lovely quiet room with a balcony. <Author>Kaza31
<Content>David  Agree with most of the other stuff on the site, so won't bother repeating things. The only points I wanted to make were that the hotel is quite expensive, although I went in October which I'm told is 'peak' season. It's worth bearing in mind that bus journies cost E1.20 each way, and two of us were spending about E7.00 each day, which needs to be weighed up with a more centrally located / posher hotel. Also, whilst all the great things reported on this site are true hence my 5* rating (especially the friendliness), the decor is quite bland / dated (think '1930's hotel' and 'Agatha Christie novel'), but I guess that lends it charm. Worth bearing in mind when you compare against some of the more chic hotels though. The breakfast is also very basic, but I guess that's minor.In terms of tips, there are 2 buses we used to take us to the hotel. The first is Bus D, and the second number 23. Both depart from immediately outside of Florence Train station. Bus D actually terminates at Piazza Ferruci, and the hotel is right across the road from there, so best to get Bus D when you first arrive. In terms of getting home after sightseeing, we found Bus 23 the best, since it departs from right outside the Duomo (cathedral) which is in the thick of the action. You need to make sure to get the bus from the street immediately outside the Duomo (left hand side when approaching the cathedral from its front) - we got the bus from just round the corner and ended up having a trip round the suburbs in the opposite direction! Get bus tickets from any tabacconist shop.We found most of the fast food lunches in Italy terrible, especially the sandwiches. We booked for 4 nights and the hotel gave us a free lunch at Borvino (next to Ponte Vecchio bridge) and this was the best and cheapest lunch we had all trip (where all the locals go) - we were sorry we only found out about it on our last day! Note: it's very hard to find so be persistent. We hated being ripped off by outside cafes - some charged E11.00 for 2 cans of Sprite!Have fun!
