<Author>BruininEurope
<Content>Away From the Crowds The Hotel David is located across the Arno outside of central Florence. Since Florence is packed with tourists in October, the location is ideal for getting away from the throngs of people. Conversely, one has to use public transportation (comfortable and readily available), taxis (expensive), or walking to get to the city. We love walking and went into Florence a variety of ways, through the Ponto Viecchio or via Santa Croce, and got to see the city up close. One warning: transporation gets real spotty after 10PM (even cabs) so be forwarned. The hotel itself is comfortable, tasteful, and a little homey. Staff are especially polite and helpful. The room was large and comfortable. There was free internet access. Breakfast offered a wide range of excellent choices. Located in a neighborhood - as opposed to a central city business district - exploring the nearby streets was interesting.

<Author>RossCobbinOZ
<Content>nice hotel- terrible location! There seem to be a lot a reviews on Trip advisor that say things like, 'so wonderful to be out of the tourist path  bustle', and to a point I agree. It is nice in a busy city to slip out of a main thoroughfare and into a delightful little street where your charming old hotel awaits your weary head. Alas- not so here!Florence is a beautiful place, but in the summer months it gets very hot and dirty, and traffic is an ever-present evil (and I mean italian traffic; of the hooting, gesticulating and dodge-for-your-life variety). The main way you find yourself getting around it by walking and, if you are to see a fraction of what this magnificent city has to offer, you will do a LOT of walking. So the very last thing you will want to do at the end of a hot and dusty day is to force your aching feet to propel you for at least another half an hour to be able to get to your hotel! The David is a nice hotel for sure, the rooms are clean, and the little amateur frescoes painted in unexpected places are quirky and charming. The staff are helpful and unassuming, (despite giving us wrong information about the opening hours of the Brancacci chapel), even if the room towels are completely inneffectual (the towel equivalent of that old fashioned shiny toilet paper- more akin to tracing paper; whose chief purpose seemed to be dispersal, rather than absorbtion).But it really is miles away from anything- and in the opposite direction to everything else, so you won't come across it on en route to anything else. In fact most tourist maps won't even have it on there. The hotel advises that you can use the buses when they come- but we found them packed, dirty and irregular. Also, after hours of sweaty sightseeing, who wants to wait twenty five minutes for a municipal bus to get you home? My other gripe is that- by all means site your hotel 'away from the action' if there is something to be gained from from it; perhaps a romantic vista of the city, or remote tranquility etc. But the David is on a hideous main road, where the honks, brake screeches and sirens are probably more pronounced than anywhere else! And as for views? Well they would be of the same road. Not a pretty sight, and not what E.M Forster would have had in mind.A nice little hotel- and fairly reasonable, but a 20 min+ walk in the baking florentine sun to the far side of the Ponte Vecchio is just not mainstream hotel territory. Nice when you're there though.  
<Date>Oct 12, 2006

<Author>Kirbly
<Content>A very special hotel We had a lovely stay in Florence, with the hotel playing a large part in our enjoyment. The hotel staff were always friendly and helpful, helping us to find out bus times for day trips and booking our tickets to the Uffizi (if you're going, it's best to request this in advance as we had to wait 2 days  go at 16:15). The staff couldn't have been more helpful, and their perfect english made things very easy. The location is about 25-30 minutes walk from the city, but buses stop very near the hotel and only cost 鈧?.20. The only reason that I haven't given 5 stars is the distance from the city and the fact that there is no hotel restaurant. The breakfasts were always great  well stocked - yoghurt, baked goods, croissants, cereal, etc, and the daily evening aperitifs were a lovely touch. Our room was large and very clean, with a fridge and air conditioning. The bathroom was also very spacious. There is also free internet use. All in all, a fantastic choice of hotel - I'd definitely recommend it highly to anyone.

<Author>rpalmer
<Content>Excellent inn on quiet side of the river My wife and I stayed at the David Hotel for one night in September 2006. We were relieved to reach the relative calm of Florence after spending three days in Rome, and we were even more relieved to find that the positive reviews of this hotel ring absolutely true. We were greeted with genuine warmth and escorted to our room on the first floor. The room was outfitted with a canopy bed, a small desk, and a large hutch/dresser. The bed was firm and comfortable. We enjoyed the fifteen minute walk into central Florence, which provided spectacular views of the Ponte Vecchio.In the evenings the hotel provides wine and light appetizers in the very pleasant lobby. Breakfast is on the second floor and consists of cold cuts, bread, yogurt, coffee, tea, and juice.We were very pleased with the friendly, personalized service, and although the location is outside of the central tourist area, we enjoyed the surroundings and would undoubtedly choose the David Hotel again if we are ever fortunate enough to return to Florence.

<Author>PAtraveler01
<Content>A jewel in Florence...what a find!! We visited Rome, Sorrento, Tuscany, Florence and Venice for two and a half weeks in early July 2006. We stayed at the Hotel David during our Florence stay and were thoroughly pleased and impressed with this hotel.The staff was second to none (they recommended restaurants that were delightful), booked us reservations at the Uffizi and Accademia in advance of our arrival (the lines would have been awful but we pretty much just walked into these museums), advised us on transport to the central historic area (it's walkable but the bus is right outside the door of the hotel and so easy to take), and made us feel welcome in so many other ways. Again, the entire staff (we interacted with at least three front desk people during our stay) was this helpful and pleaseant -- how nice!The hotel itself had very nice rooms that were clean, roomy, air conditioned and had nice bathroom. The rooms were impeccably clean and the chambermaid kept it that way every day. Not overly fancy, but just fine for us.In the early evening the hotel puts out various canapes and other finger-foods, wines and juices so the guests can chat and relax in the wonderul lobby area. This area was so pleasant, with all types of travel books, a chess board, sofas and chairs and an outside oasis to unwind from a busy day of sightseeing. They also grant all guests access (at no cost) to a lobby computer so you can check your e-mail, etc.)Breakfast was very nice -- cappucino, espresso, american coffee, hot chocolate, yogurts, cheeses, meats, pastries, fresh fruits, etc. We were at the hotel for three days and had enough variety to keep it new each day. The location in my mind was a nice benefit. Close enough to the central historical district to easily catch a bus in (or walk) but far enough to be away from the hoards of tourists, etc. It was a welcome respite to relax at the hotel after a hot and busy day of doing tourist stuff in Florence.This hotel is a find! It has all of the charm, service and comfort that we needed or desired. BTW, my wife accidently left a piece of jewelry on the vanity in the bathroom upon our departure. When we called from Venice they located the jewelry and mailed it to us back in the U.S. (without even asking for reimbursement!!) . It arrived within a week of us returning home. That's special!!So, if you're looking for a really nice place to stay while enjoying Florence then look no further!! We know where we'll be staying next time we visit Florence and where we'll suggest our friends stay when they visit -- Hotel David!!!

<Author>MtnMama
<Content>What A Find! We (two adults, two teen boys) booked the David Hotel based on reviews here and we weren't disappointed. It's lovely and peaceful and the staff is friendly and helpful. The public areas of the hotel are beautifully decorated with antiques and we loved the wall decorations that follow you up the staircase. We especially loved the door into the breakfast room! We booked two double rooms at the beginning of our travels and returned at the end of our trip to stay in a quad room. All the rooms were unique, attractively decorated, comfortable and clean. It was very hot during our stay (late June /early July 2006) and the quiet, efficient air conditioning was quite welcome. The internet access was appreciated by all. The social hour in the evening was a wonderful way to transition from day to night and the staff has some great recommendations for restaurants. If you don't feel like venturing far, try the rosticceria one street over (toward the river). They have a gorgeous deli case, are helpful and friendly, and there were many locals taking out both times we went there. They had cooked meats, fish, pasta and rice, pizza, vegetable dishes (try the eggplant wrapped in prosciutto) as well as wine and beer to take out. They also supply napkins and utensils. We took our meal back to the Hotel David and sat at the large table in the garden. We fed a family of four for 20 euro including wine! The fact that the Hotel David is a bit of a walk from the center of town may be a deterrent for some, but we really liked the fact that we were out of the hub-bub. If you're driving in Tuscany the David is a perfect place to stay as it's at a major crossroads and there's parking on-site. For those without a car, a bus stop AND a taxi stand are located just outside the hotel gate. We used both at various times. I think a taxi ride to the Duomo/Accademia was about 5 or 6 euro for four of us and took about 10 minutes. But mostly we walked in and out from the city center and really enjoyed it. We loved our stay at the David and highly recommend it.  
<Date>Jul 14, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful Stay! I just arrived home from a 16 day trip to Italy. We spent 4 nights at the Hotel David and were very happy that we did. It is a little gem on the Oltrarno side of the Arno. It is a lovely, scenic 10 minute walk to the Uffizi and a little less to Santa Croce. The bus line, though, is right outside the door of the hotel (the D bus and the 23) so if you are a bit tired of walking (or hot, it was 96 degrees when we were there this June!) you can just hop on a bus.  The hotel itself is so welcoming. Our group had 4 different rooms, 2 singles,a double and a triple, all but one with terraces. We were all very pleased with our accomodations. The triple had beautiful Florentine furniture and beds and a deep soaking tub, which was such a pleasure on a hot day. The common rooms are lovely and you can play chess or cards or quietly read a book. There are also many art books and travel guides to browse through. Each evening at 6:30 there are snacks and wine in the main lobby and it is fun to talk to the other guests, The staff are very helpful with anything you may want: restaurant recomendations, museum tickets, directions etc. The breakfasts were quite good, too.I have no reservation in recommending the Hotel David and I would stay here again.

<Author>fxavier
<Content>Everything we expected and more We (two couples) spent four nights at this wonderful hotel the second week in June. We instructed our travel agent to book us into the Hotel David after having read the previous reviews on this website. We were not disappointed. In fact, it was the best property we stayed in during our two week trip to Italy, and we stayed in some very nice hotels. The staff is extremely helpful with directions, dining suggestions and any other major or minor thing you might want. The breakfasts are great, the rooms are large as are the bathrooms and there is a wonderful little spread put our every afternoon for the guests with wine and little snacks. This hotel is not in the middle of Florence -- something we appreciated, but if you don't want to walk (10 or 15 minutes) or take public transportation or a taxi, this might not be your favorite. However, there are plenty of restaurants and shopping on the other side of the Arno, of which we took great advantage. The hotel is close to Piazz Michelangelo, which gives visitors great views of the city especially at sunset and is close to the Pitti Palace and Boboli Gardens.

<Author>Jol
<Content>Loved the Hotel David Just returned from our first trip to Italy. We spent 5 nights at the David at the end of May and found it as good as the reviews suggest or better. We had arranged for the hotel shuttle to meet us at the airport after our long flight and were greeted by the welcoming smile of the young owner. He runs a most efficient,immaculate hotel with helpful staff and extra touches. In the comfortable and spacious common areas, furnished with lovely antiques, there is a generous collection of guide books and interesting magazines for use of the guests. Internet access was welcome, and we enjoyed breakfast in the bright room run by a cheerful young woman.There are cheerful modern wall frescoes in the hallways. We were in room 11, a double on the 2nd floor with a big balcony with flower boxes overlooking the garden and screened by trees which provide complete privacy. Unfortunately they don't protect from the constant traffic noise. Those motor scooter drivers can get amazing decibels out of their machines! The minibar was kept replenished, the linens changed daily, and we got used to the flat, no-pile towels which actually dry you very well, kind of like blotting paper! Although the hotel is a bit away from the heart of the action, we found that an advantage and hopped on the D bus to get to and fro or walked. There are only two nearby restaurants, and at the one we tried, Trattoria l'Orologio, we were served by a supercilious creep wearing electric blue glasses. He was just too cool for the likes of us! We did find two other pleasant restaurants in Oltrarno - Osteria del Cingale Bianco, and Casalinga. We would be happy to stay at the David again and recommend it highly.

<Author>artemis1
<Content>Nice little hotel We are just back from 3 nights at this hotel. The rooms were spacious and comfortable, and the bathroom fine too. It was all very clean. Our room felt a little dark as there were lots of trees outside the window but I suspect in the heat of summer this would be a godsend. Not too sure about the soundproofing. We never heard anyone else admittedly but the person in the room next to us liked to have loud conversations on the phone at 1am and 6am. Not very conducive to sleeping!Breakfast was ok, but nothing to rave about. I was surprised having read so many good reviews about the breakfasts. It was adequate but nothing special. it set us up for a day's walkign though.The hotel is in a nice little place, away from the hustle and bustle. We did enjoy our walk along the river every day to get into the city proper, and it was perhaps only 10 minutes to walk up to the Piazza Michaelangelo for great views of the city. Ignore the hoards of tourists and soak up the views. We would be more than happy to stay in this hotel again.

<Content>Bellisimo Just returned from 5 nights @ David. From the moment we arrived at the hotel it was a perfect stay. The staff was great, very friendly and professional. The hotel is small and quaint, an old villa that has been refurbished w/ 25 rooms. The common space had large open spaces w/ travel books  papers,free internet service and reasonable bar prices. We had room 15 which was a triple, front facing,large, airy and very clean(actually it is in the brochure and exactly as shown)It is on the 3rd floor. Double pain windows keep out noise at night. The breakfast was served in a bright and breezy room and fully stocked thanks to Maria. She will make you a latte or any other coffee you wish. Evenings they put out appetizers and wine so guests can mingle. The garden is great to read and have a glass of wine. April is the best month to travel..not to hot and no bugs.For us the best thing about David was the location and personal service. We liked being away from the hordes of tourists and being in a residential area. Also-the size of the hotel allows for boutique style and great service. The guests we met were from all around the globe and seasoned travlers. It was wonderful to trade stories and get ideas from others.We also used Roberto (Allesandro's colleage) for a private tour thru Tuscany. What a day!!Great places to eat all around hotel. Our favorite picks: L'Orologio (across street,great food,aloof service until they get to know you) Gigi on Via G. Orsisni (3 blocks from hotel) Affe di Bacco-go down Via Orsini and make a right before Gigi on Via di Rusciano. Excellent pasta  pizza and lastly Trattoria Peppino on Via G. Orsini (2 blocks past Gigi). Last tip: take the Sightseeing Firenze double decker bus that picks up 2 blocks from hotel that you can hop on/off at all locations-great way to see everything. ALso goes to Fiesole. Grazie to Gabrielle, Serena, Michaela  Chiara for a great stay. A presto

<Author>Tulsan
<Content>Our new Favorite Hotel! Thanks so much to all of you who took the time to recommend this jewel that seems to get omitted from all of the guidebooks! You were absolutely right! <Author>monamia
<Content>Hotel David: Fantastic Everything What a great little hotel. Beautiful accommodations, roomy room with nice bath, inviting parlor areas, full library of Italy travel books, maps and more, free and easy Internet access; knowledgeable, charming, accommodating reception personnel. What a great experience. They helped me plot my way from Florence to the airport in Rome, secure Uffizi reservations, and so many wonderful recommendations. It is like having friends in Florence to have stayed there, and so perfect and completely comfortable for a woman travelling solo. Family-friendly as well. Wonderful guests were a pleasure to meet for travel chat; sophisticated, experienced travellers.I loved the area. It is in a lovely neighborhood, a short, convenient bus ride away. Visitors can get a flavor of a nice Florentine neighborhood, very well-located. A rotiscerria across the street, with charming English speaking proprietors, is perfect for a dinner to go of healthy roasted chicken and grilled vegetables, pasta side dishes, affordable bottled water! Excellent price and quality; a trattoria is right next door, but our wonderful hosts will make you a quick cappuchino as well, and easily conjure up stronger spirits for those who wish. Evening features an apertif drop-in reception in the hotel parlor, which is lovely, and hospitable, but also with private, quiet space for reading and relaxing. What a great, great place! Very residential in style. I will go and stay again.Thanks to those who took time to post their comments on Hotel David. You helped make my trip terrific. I found the Hotel David by reading reviews here and noting its staggeringly high satisfaction ratings for a smaller boutique hotel. I stayed five nights and would love to be there still. This is not the hotel for those who wish to immerse themselves in the crowded, polluted chaos of the tourist scene; in fact, I avoided the Duomo, Accademia areas as best I could. The Oltrarno area will forever be my strong preference for a home-base. I enjoyed my walks in and out of town, weaving up and down different streets, but a bus stop is right there if that is needed. Don't miss the pleasure of a quick bus trip up the road to San Miniato, good chance to see some fine local villas and lush flora. Above the inferior and well-populated Piazza Michelangelo view.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Keep the Location In Mind The hotel was nice, I would just caution fellow travelers about the location - it was too far to walk to the historical core multiple times in a day. For instance, running back to the hotel to take a nap or drop off packages, pick up or drop off a jacket or umbrella was not really practical and was time consuming. I thought the walk would be no problem and would be enjoyable along the river, we're young 40's - but the reality was that you are walking along a road with lots of noise and exhaust fumes and you need your energy to walk all around town once you get there. (In addition to walking, we did take the bus many times, but at night it stopped running pretty early like 9:00 or 10:00.) If I had a car that I needed to park for my stay in Florence - then I think it would be a fine choice. But, for myself, I now have a new travel rule, which I picked up from this trip to Italy, (from stays in Sienna, Lucca and Florence) if you are only there for a few days and have no car, stay in the city center and within the town walls, even if it costs more or is a less desirable hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hotel David Is A Great Find We liked this hotel a lot. It is a vintage Italian house just outside of downtown Florence, a good walk (15 minute) or short bus ride away from the Uffizi, Duomo and other sites. It was quite reasonably priced compared with other downtown hotels, and since it it an old Florentine mansion, the rooms were very spacious and tastefully, if simply, appointed. The bathroom was large and with gorgeous Italian tile walls and floor. The staff was very attentive and helpful, with good English, and the nice breakfast was served in a beautiful second-floor room. There was also a great sitting area with comfortable chairs and sofas and a lot of reading material in both English and Italian. Finally, there is a self-serve Laundromat just down the street that was very handy after traveling for a week with our four-person family. 2 loads of laundry and 3 dryer cycles ran around 17 Euros, but that pales in comparison to what it would have cost to send out laundry from a hotel, and only took about 1-1/2 hours. We would definitely stay there again.  
<Date>Apr 19, 2005

<Author>Boink
<Content>Fantastic Deal in Florence First rate. The is a classic, old hotel... with a comfortable lobby and excellent staff (that speak fluent English and were more than happy to get reservations for museums). We stayed in Room 11 (on the 3rd floor) which is a corner room facing the front of the hotel with a terrace (and en-suite). The room was spacious and the bathroom was fine (though only a shower). The breakfast was good. This is a really fantastic deal for Florence (84 Euros). The only drawback is the location, but this really isn't a serious matter. It is a 15 minute walk to the heart of things (maybe 20), but it's a nice walk along the Arno toward the Ponte Vecchio... and there are several easy-to-catch buses that frequenty come and go if one wanted to do that. The hotel is in a quiet neighborhood on the south bank of the Arno and a bit east of the old part of the city. There aren't a lot of restaurant options in the area, but most go to the heart of the old city anyway. Again, the distance is probably what allows for the price of the stay, but we (age middle-50s) had no problems at all with the location.A great deal in a fine establishment.

<Author>Lynda
<Content>We can't wait to go back Let me add to the rave reviews! We'd booked thro' venere (where you can read lots more) and notified on booking that we were travelling with relatives aged over 80. The e-mail had been noted and they had been allocated double with bathtub with shower on same floor as breakfast room, while we were in the triple above (shower only). Large, light rooms with parquet floors. From the moment of arrival onwards all the staff were friendly and helpful, on one occasion even looking up (unasked) curent opening times for the cathedral and printing them off for us.They also have a good (multilingual) stock of guidebooks for you to consult, as well as Int. Herald Tribune, Italian papers, and news magazines.We liked the walk along the river to ponte vecchio with skyline of duomo and towers to accompany you.We only took bus once to get to Accademia in time to join queue to pick up reserved tickets. We'd stayed in Oltrarno before ( at Hotel Boboli, which we would NOT recommend!) and liked being away from the tourist bustle. We ate 3 nights at the trattoria L'Orologio across the road (next to bus-stop): good choice for lighter supper or full meal. Food very good, service less so! The last night we walked to Gigli (recommended by hotel): slightly more expensive (mainly full meals). The free parking had been a major factor in our booking (we'd toured Tuscany and Umbria and kept the car to do day-trip to Pisa/Lucca and to get back to airport) as it saved us 100 euros compared with other hotels. The hotel in the event exceeded our expectations for a 3-star by miles: it features in a guide of hotels with charm and it's clear why. A final image: a crackling fire in the salon on a freezing February evening (and all those nibbles while you enjoy it).

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfect Hotel Just came back from Florence on Oct12. This hotel is perfect for the price. Got more than my money's worth for 98E triple per night. In Italy, this is cheap. Located in a shady area down the hill from Piazza Michelangelo where everyone goes for the magnificent view of the town of Florence. It has beautiful garden and parking. The hotel is accessible to bus which is only across the street. Bus D is great if you want to stop and start your walk from Ponte Vecchio to the main center. Hotel David's location is more quiet than other hotels in the downtown area of Florence where you can hear scooters and buses pass by while you sleep at night. The rooms are quiet and large, has high ceiling, beds are comfortable, smells clean, floors are clean, as well as bathroom. The complimentary snack that they serve at around 630pm is so nice. The staff, was very helpful, specially Serena, who has the great, sweet smile. She's refreshing. All the restaurants they recommended are excellent. Trattoria Beppino, which is a few blocks away on Via de Ripoli are highly recommended. This place is not your typical restaurant that serve tourists menu. Locals come here to eat!! Check it out! Get there early at 730pm or better yet get reservations from the hotel staff. I will go back to this hotel again and will recommend to all. Hotel David, you made my stay in Florence pleasurable. Thank you.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Charming Hotel My family - 2 adults/2 kids - stayed here Good Friday and Saturday nights in April 2004. We drove into Florence from the north (I do not recommend), and finding the hotel was a little tricky - streets are not labeled well in Italy! The staff was very helpful and friendly. The room on the first floor was very large- A king size bed plus two twin beds. Bathroom included a shower and was warm. We did not hear any street noise or noise from other rooms or the lobby - and we were right off the lobby. Breakfast included meat and cheese with yogurt, juice, rolls, etc. They did not charge us for hot chocolate or water. The internet access was wonderful - my husband could catch up on work matters and my teenage daughter loved instant messaging her friends. Another bonus is that they provide parking for free. The few drawbacks were minimal - there was a smell of cigarette smoke in the room and a strong smell in the lobby. In addition, the hotel is located in an area with few restaurants - although the rotisserie across the street was fantastic, as was the restaurant down the street that the hotel recommended. There are also grocery stores nearby. Finally, the hotel is located outside the historic district - but only a 10 minute or so walk along the Arno. You could take a quick taxi or a bus outside the hotel. We felt the hotel was a steal at 140 euros for a quad. We would stay there again.
